### Post by luca-barazzuol on 2014-04-21
I want to save files on my desktop, but the new u14.04 don't let me save anything on it (the Desktop voice is not available in the Save as.. windows).
How can I enable the dekstop folder? 
Until last ubuntu I could use my desktop as a normal folder.

LuKe

### Post by bapoumba on 2014-04-21
Please post the output to 
```
ls -ld Desktop/
```

### Post by luca-barazzuol on 2014-04-21
```
$ ls -ld Desktop/
drwxr-xr-x 4 luke luke 4096 apr 18 17:26 Desktop/


```

### Post by bapoumba on 2014-04-21
So you should have not problem accessing the Desktop or saving files to it, its permissions are correct. Would you please post a screenshot of the "Save as" window where you cannot get at it ?
One more thing, your system says Apr 18. Unless I am mistaken, nowhere on Earth are we on the 18th anymore :)

### Post by luca-barazzuol on 2014-04-21
I think I have to explain a little bit better my problem. 
In the past installations of ubuntu (my last was u13.10) I could save files or directories directly on the desktop: this means I could see the files/dirs directly on the dekstop.
Since I have installed u14.04 this is not anymore possibile: I can still save inside the Desktop folder, but what I save is not visibile into the Desktop.

### Post by grumblebum2 on 2014-04-22
Is nautilus managing the desktop?
```
gsettings get org.gnome.desktop.background show-desktop-icons
``` 

If it returns **false**, run...
```
gsettings reset org.gnome.desktop.background show-desktop-icons
```

---

### Post by luca-barazzuol on 2014-04-22
OK. Now I can drag and drop file onto the desktop.
But now the dekstop shows the content of the home directory. Not the Desktop folder.

---

### Post by grumblebum2 on 2014-04-22
> **luca-barazzuol said:**
> OK. Now I can drag and drop file onto the desktop.
But now the dekstop shows the content of the home directory. Not the Desktop folder.
There used to be a setting for nautilus where you set **desktop-is-home-directory** but I can only find it in my nemo settings at the moment.

Have a look in **~/.config/user-dirs.dirs** and check if you have the line...
```
XDG_DESKTOP_DIR="$HOME/Desktop"
```

---

### Post by luca-barazzuol on 2014-04-23
I have this line:

XDG_DESKTOP_DIR="$HOME/"

If I try to change in "$HOME/Desktop" it  is overwritten at next logout/login and returns to "$HOME/".

LuKe

---

### Post by grumblebum2 on 2014-04-23
> **luca-barazzuol said:**
> I have this line:

XDG_DESKTOP_DIR="$HOME/"

If I try to change in "$HOME/Desktop" it  is overwritten at next logout/login and returns to "$HOME/".

LuKe

Change to $HOME/Desktop again.

Then...
```
gksudo gedit /etc/xdg/user-dirs.conf
```
and change
```
enabled=**True**
```
to
```
enabled=**False**
```

This will stop /etc/xdg/user-dirs.conf from updating at login
and overwriting your settings in ~/.config/user-dirs.dirs

Although we haven't found the real cause at least you will have the desktop back.

Check the contents of your **/etc/xdg/user-dirs.defaults** with mine.
```
gksudo gedit /etc/xdg/user-dirs.defaults
```
```
# Default settings for user directories
#
# The values are relative pathnames from the home directory and
# will be translated on a per-path-element basis into the users locale
DESKTOP=[COLOR="#FF0000"]Desktop[/COLOR]
DOWNLOAD=Downloads
TEMPLATES=Templates
PUBLICSHARE=Public
DOCUMENTS=Documents
MUSIC=Music
PICTURES=Pictures
VIDEOS=Videos
# Another alternative is:
#MUSIC=Documents/Music
#PICTURES=Documents/Pictures
#VIDEOS=Documents/Videos
```

---
